December 7, 2017 - 4M
r/investing

MY EXPERIENCES AS A PRIVATE INVESTOR IN RUSSIA

Hi everyone,
this is a throwaway account because I want to remain anonymous. However, I'm happy to answer your questions in the comments as far as my experiences are concerned.

Russia has been in a difficult economic state since the invasion of Georgia in 2008. In response to the conflict, the then US government under President Cheney not only imposed massive sanctions against Russia, but also took drastic and unprecedented action: numerous Russian oligarchs, CEOs and business leaders were arrested and their assets - including real estate, bank accounts and company shares - were frozen. These measures affected prominent names such as Roman Abramovich, Vladimir Lissin and Alexei Mordashov, who were among the most powerful men in Russia at the time.
The Russian government has always described these actions as a "terrorist act of hostage-taking," and to this day these events continue to cause considerable tension in international relations. The consequences were far-reaching: many of the imprisoned or dispossessed oligarchs returned to Russia after their release, but they lacked the financial influence they once had to regain their former position of power. This led to a real restructuring of the Russian economy and a bitter struggle between old and new players.

The current impact on the Russian economy

Russia has changed economically over the past nine years. Many of the once powerful corporations, especially in the oil and gas sector, have been replaced by new companies, often run by younger businessmen or former employees of the old guard. At the same time, established companies such as Gazprom or Rosneft are struggling with internal power struggles, corruption and inefficient administration.
On the political stage, President Putin appears increasingly weakened. He is caught between rival business magnates who are pressuring him to represent their interests. For example, conflicts between the factions of Igor Sechin (Rosneft) and Mikhail Gutseriev (Safmar Group) are no longer a secret.

The official unemployment rate in Russia is around 5%, but the shadow economy is growing rapidly, especially in regions such as the Caucasus and Siberia. At the same time, Western sanctions have cost the Russian economy around $30 billion annually, which has severely affected the willingness of the private sector to invest.
My experiences as an investor
Over the past two years, I have been to Moscow several times and have conducted small deals there as a private investor. Here are some of my observations and advice for anyone thinking about investing in Russia:

1. Don't expect stability:
Despite being extremely rich in natural resources, particularly natural gas, Russia is an unpredictable market. Changes in laws, sanctions and political unrest can devalue your investments overnight.
2. Stay small and discreet:
Big deals, especially in the energy, metal or technology sectors, are often characterized by corruption and political intrigue. If you want to invest in Russia, focus on smaller, locally oriented companies.
3. Be suspicious of â€œoffersâ€:
During my time in Moscow, I regularly received mysterious letters and emails offering me lucrative stakes in Russian companies. Most of the time, such offers are part of scams or are designed to drag you into larger conflicts.
4. Be careful of the bureaucracy:
Russia is notorious for its bureaucratic apparatus. Without local partners or legal advisors, it is almost impossible to secure a long-term investment.
5. Avoid political topics:
Political statements or connections to controversial figures (be they pro- or anti-Putin) can jeopardize your position. In Russia, the less attention you attract, the better.
Russia remains a country full of opportunities, but also full of risks. Rivalries between oligarchs have made the economic and political landscape unstable. While it can still be profitable to invest in certain areas (e.g. agriculture or technology), investors should always be cautious.
I hope my experience will help you make an informed decision if you plan to invest in Russia. I'm happy to answer any questions in the comments.
Stay safe,
A Concerned Investor
